Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition where breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep.
  It is caused by a blockage of the airway, usually when the soft tissue in the back of the throat collapses during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor of the jaw that can cause swelling and pain, but not obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Dentigerous cyst is a type of cyst that forms around an unerupted tooth, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Orbital fracture is a break in the bone surrounding the eye, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint is fused, which can cause difficulty opening the mouth and obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

  However, the most common number of segments in dentistry is four, one for each quadrant of the mouth.

Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient had a myocardial infarction 2 weeks back.
  The lipid profile shows HDL 32 mg/dL, LDL 126 mg/dL, and TG 276 mg/dL.
  The patient has high TG levels and low HDL levels.
  The preferred treatment for this patient is a fibrate.
  Rosuvastatin is a statin and is not the preferred treatment for this patient.
  Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose and may not be necessary for this patient.
  Therefore, the best choice is A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.
Action: Answer("A")

  Option A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate is the preferred treatment for this patient.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal vaccine that protects against 23 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are at high risk of pneumococcal infections.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are also at high risk of pneumococcal infections.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may have a bacterial infection caused by pneumococcal bacteria.
  Children less than 2 years are also at high risk of pneumococcal infections.
  Therefore, PPV-23 is most beneficial for all of the given options.
Action: Answer("E") - None of the above.
Response 1:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal vaccine that protects against 23 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are also at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may benefit from the vaccine, but they are not at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Children less than 2 years old are not recommended to receive PPV-23.
  Therefore, the most beneficial group for PPV-23 is either A or B.

Choices:

  B: Vaginal hysterectomy
  C: Fothergill repair
  D: Manchester operation

  LSCS stands for Lower Segment Caesarean Section, which is a surgical procedure to deliver a baby through an incision in the mother's abdomen and uterus.

  B: Quadritubercular teeth

  A: MMR
  B: HIV conjugate polysaccharide vaccine
  C: Typhoid Vi polysaccharide vaccine
  D: Influenza vaccine

  MMR vaccine is a combination vaccine that protects against measles, mumps, and rubella.
  HIV conjugate polysaccharide vaccine is not a vaccine that is commonly used.
  Typhoid Vi polysaccharide vaccine is a vaccine that protects against typhoid fever.
  Influenza vaccine is a vaccine that protects against the flu.
  ITP has been reported as a rare complication of the MMR vaccine.
  Therefore, the answer is A: MMR.

Topic: Pediatrics
Question: Short child with low T4 and raised TSH and swelling of pituitary, what is the diangosis ?
Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Thought:
  Low T4 and raised TSH indicate hypothyroidism.
  Swelling of the pituitary gland suggests a pituitary tumor.
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a type of pituitary tumor that causes hyperthyroidism.
  TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder that causes hypothyroidism.
  Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is a pituitary tumor causing secondary hypothyroidism.
Action: Answer("B")

  Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is a pituitary tumor causing secondary hypothyroidism.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 23 of 100 ###
Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are procedures done to treat the pulp of the tooth.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in the mouth.
  Primary teeth have different characteristics than permanent teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity in the young is a characteristic of primary teeth.
  Odontoblasts are cells that form dentin, which is the hard tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth.
  Therefore, increased odontoblastic activity in the young is a reason why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  The answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are procedures that involve the removal of the pulp tissue.
  Primary teeth have a higher success rate for these procedures.
  The reason for this is because of the increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
  Odontoblasts are cells that form dentin, which is the hard tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure that involves removing the entire pulp from the tooth, while pulp capping is a procedure that involves placing a medicament over an exposed pulp to encourage healing and prevent further damage.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in a child's mouth and are eventually replaced by permanent teeth.
  Primary teeth have a wider pulp chamber and thinner dentin walls than permanent teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity in the young is a characteristic of primary teeth.

Question: Naive T cell get activated by:
Choices:
  A: NK cell
  B: Dendritic cell
  C: Macrophage
  D: B-lymphocyte
Response 0:
Thought:
  Naive T cells are T cells that have not yet encountered their specific antigen.
  Naive T cells need to be activated by an antigen-presenting cell (APC) to become effector T cells.
  NK cells are part of the innate immune system and do not present antigens to T cells.
  Macrophages can present antigens to T cells, but they are not the most efficient APCs.
  B-lymphocytes present antigens to helper T cells, but they do not activate naive T cells directly.
  Dendritic cells are the most efficient APCs and are responsible for activating naive T cells.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Dendritic cell.

Choices:
  A: B>A>D>C
  B: B>D>C>A
  C: A>D>B>C
  D: C>A>B>D

  The cochlear nucleus is the first structure in the auditory pathway that receives input from the ear.
  The inferior colliculus is located in the midbrain and receives input from the cochlear nucleus.
  The medial geniculate body is located in the thalamus and receives input from the inferior colliculus.
  The auditory cortex is the final destination of the auditory pathway.

  Biotin is a coenzyme that is required for carboxylase enzymes to function.
  Carboxylase enzymes are responsible for adding a carboxyl group to a substrate.
  Therefore, the enzyme whose activity is affected by biotin deficiency is a carboxylase enzyme.
  The answer is D: Carboxylase.

Question: Embalming without issuing death ceificate is punishable under section:
Choices:
  A: IPC 201
  B: IPC 297
  C: IPC 299
  D: IPC 498
Response 0:
Thought:
  Embalming is the process of preserving a dead body.
  A death certificate is a legal document issued by a doctor that certifies the cause of death.
  Issuing a death certificate is a legal requirement before embalming a dead body.
  Therefore, embalming without issuing a death certificate is illegal.
  To find out the section under which this act is punishable, we need to refer to the Indian Penal Code (IPC).
  After checking the IPC, the correct answer is B: IPC 297.
Action: Answer("B")

Thought:
  Embalming is the process of preserving a dead body.

  To find the answer, we need to know which section of the Indian Penal Code (IPC) deals with this offense.
  After researching, I found that IPC 297 deals with the offense of causing hurt to a person with the intent to commit or to conceal the commission of an offense.
  IPC 299 deals with culpable homicide not amounting to murder.
  IPC 498 deals with the offense of cruelty by a husband or his relatives towards a married woman.
  IPC 201 deals with the offense of causing the disappearance of evidence of an offense.
  None of the sections mentioned above deals with the offense of embalming without issuing a death certificate.
  Therefore, the answer is "None of the Above".

Question: Which of the following are the predominant connective tissue cells of the periodontal Ligament?

  A: Cementoblasts
  B: Fibroblasts
  C: Osteoblasts
  D: Rests of Malassez

  B: Lymphatics
  C: Blood vessels
  D: Aspiration of tumor cells

Response 5:
Thought:
  Metastasis is the spread of cancer cells from one part of the body to another.
  Oral cancer is a type of cancer that can occur in any part of the mouth.
  The oral cavity has a rich lymphatic network.
  Lymphatic vessels are thin tubes that branch, like blood vessels, throughout the body.
  Lymphatic vessels carry lymph, a colorless, watery fluid that contains infection-fighting cells called lymphocytes.
  Lymphatic vessels drain into lymph nodes, small, bean-shaped structures that filter out harmful substances.
  Cancer cells can break away from the primary tumor and travel through the lymphatic system to nearby or distant lymph nodes.
  Therefore, the most common route for metastasis of oral cancer is by B: Lymphatics.
Action: Answer("B")

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 40 of 100 ###
Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone and cementum.
  If the root surface has been exposed for 6 years, it is likely that the PDL fibres have been lost.
  Therefore, the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
  The answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves cutting and moving a section of gum tissue to expose the tooth root.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the tooth roots have been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibres are periodontal ligament fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  Cementum is a layer of hard, mineralized tissue that covers the tooth root.
  Dentin is a hard, mineralized tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the tooth root.
  Co adaptation refers to the process of the tooth and surrounding tissues adapting to changes in the environment.
  Based on this information, the most likely answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves cutting and moving a section of gum tissue to expose the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the tooth roots have been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibres are periodontal ligament fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  The PDL fibers are attached to the cementum, which is the outer layer of the tooth root.
  Therefore, a lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show PDL fibres attached to cementum.
  The answer is A: PDL fibres attached to cementum.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves the reflection of a flap of gingival tissue to expose the underlying tooth root.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibres are fibers that attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  In a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibres are expected to be lost.
  Therefore, the answer is not A or B.
  Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is expected to be present.
  Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is not expected.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.

Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
  All of the given options are lipoproteins.
  Lipoproteins are complexes of lipids and proteins.
  The density of lipoproteins increases as the proportion of protein increases.
  Chylomicrons have the highest proportion of lipids and the lowest proportion of protein.
  Therefore, Chylomicrons have the least density.
Action: Answer("D")

  Lipoproteins are complexes of lipids and proteins.

Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The Bishop score is used to assess the readiness of the cervix for induction of labor.
  The score is based on five components: cervical dilation, cervical effacement, cervical consistency, cervical position, and fetal station.
  The maximum score is 13, and a score of 8 or higher indicates that the cervix is favorable for induction.
  In this case, the cervix is 1 cm dilated, 30% effaced, soft, and posterior, and the fetal station is -1.
  Therefore, the modified Bishop score for this lady will be 5.

Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
  Malocclusion is a condition where the teeth are not properly aligned.
  Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population with a particular condition at a specific point in time.
  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a condition in a population over a specific period of time.
  Morbidity refers to the state of being diseased or unhealthy within a population.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.

  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a specific condition in a population over a given period of time.
  Morbidity refers to the state of being diseased or unhealthy within a population.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Since the question is asking about the proportion of individuals in a population with a specific condition at a given time, the best answer is A: Prevalence rate.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 9:

  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a specific condition in a population over a specific period of time.

Question: Iron entry into enterocytes occurs which of the following?
Choices:
  A: DMT-1
  B: Ferropoin
  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin

  Iron entry into enterocytes is the first step in iron absorption.

  Ferropoin is not a known protein involved in iron absorption.
  Transferrin is a protein that binds iron in the blood and transports it to cells.
  Hepcidin is a hormone that regulates iron metabolism by controlling the amount of iron that is absorbed from the diet.
  Therefore, the correct answer is A: DMT-1.

Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummers classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is a classification system used to describe the complexity of root canal systems.
  Multi constricted apical constriction refers to the presence of multiple narrow apical foramina.
  Type 1 in Dummer's classification refers to a single, straight root canal.
  Type 2 refers to two separate canals that join into one canal.
  Type 3 refers to two separate canals that remain separate throughout the length of the root.
  Type 4 refers to multiple canals and multiple foramina.
  Since multi constricted apical constriction refers to the presence of multiple foramina, it is most likely to be seen in Type 4.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought:
  Dummer's classification is used to classify the root canal system.
  Multi constricted apical constriction means that there are multiple constrictions at the apex of the root.
  Type 1 has a single canal that extends from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  Type 2 has two canals that join into one canal before exiting the apex.
  Type 3 has three or more canals that join into one canal before exiting the apex.
  Type 4 has multiple separate canals that exit the apex.
  Multi constricted apical constriction is not mentioned in the descriptions of Type 1, Type 2, or Type 4.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Type 3.

  B: Secondary caries

  D: Rampant caries

  Recurrent caries occur around existing fillings or sealants.
  Rampant caries is a severe and rapidly progressing decay that affects multiple teeth.

  Therefore, the answer is A: Initial caries.

  A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney

  C: Thirst center in the hypothalamus
  D: Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus
Response 0:
Thought:
Antidiuretic hormone (ADH) is also known as vasopressin.
ADH is produced in the hypothalamus and released from the posterior pituitary gland.
ADH regulates water balance in the body by acting on the kidneys.
ADH increases water reabsorption in the kidneys by acting on the collecting ducts.
Therefore, the primary site of action of antidiuretic hormone is on the distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.
The answer is A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.

  D: Fluoride application

  Endodontic treatment is not recommended for primary teeth.
  Extraction is not the first line of treatment for primary teeth.
  Restoration is the treatment of choice for S-ECC.
  Fluoride application is a preventive measure and not a treatment for S-ECC.
  Therefore, the line of treatment for this patient is restoration.

  The answer is B: Restoration.

Topic: Pathology
Question: Which of the following may be a feature of acromegaty?
Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a hormonal disorder that results from excessive growth hormone (GH) production.
  The excess GH production is usually caused by a benign tumor of the pituitary gland.
  The condition is characterized by the enlargement of hands, feet, and facial features.
  A large tongue is a feature of acromegaly.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, which is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Crowded teeth is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Large tongue.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a disorder caused by excess growth hormone (GH) production.
  GH stimulates growth in bones and tissues.
  Therefore, acromegaly may cause enlargement of bones and tissues.
  A large tongue is a feature of acromegaly.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, which is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly, but rather hyperglycemia (high blood sugar) due to insulin resistance.
  Crowded teeth is not a feature of acromegaly.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Large tongue.

Topic: Dental
Question: Object permanence seen in which stage of Jean Piagets theory
Choices:
  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage
Response 0:
Thought:
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they cannot be seen, heard, or touched.
  Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development describes four stages of cognitive development.
  The sensorimotor stage is the first stage of Piaget's theory, which occurs from birth to age two.
  During this stage, infants learn about the world through their senses and motor activities.
  Object permanence is a major achievement of the sensorimotor stage.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Sensorimotor.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Forensic Medicine
Question: Which of the following principles governs biomedical research in human subjects?
Choices:
  A: Geneva declaration
  B: Helsinki declaration
  C: Hippocratic oath
  D: International code of medical ethics
Response 0:
Thought:
  The question is asking about the principles that govern biomedical research in human subjects.
  The Hippocratic Oath is an oath of ethics historically taken by physicians.
  The Geneva Declaration is a declaration of the World Medical Association (WMA) that outlines the physician's dedication to the humanitarian goals of medicine.
  The International Code of Medical Ethics is a set of ethical principles for the medical profession.
  The Helsinki Declaration is a set of ethical principles regarding human experimentation developed for the medical community by the World Medical Association (WMA).
  The Helsinki Declaration is the most relevant to the question as it specifically addresses biomedical research in human subjects.
Action: Answer("B")

  The Helsinki Declaration is a set of ethical principles regarding human experimentation developed for the medical community by the World Medical Association (WMA).

  The Helsinki Declaration is the most relevant to the question as it specifically deals with biomedical research in human subjects.

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Proteinuria is a common sign of preeclampsia.
  Severe preeclampsia is diagnosed when blood pressure is greater than or equal to 160/110 mmHg and proteinuria is greater than or equal to 5 grams in a 24-hour urine sample.
  5 grams is equivalent to 5000 mg.
  Therefore, the answer is not A, B, or C.
  The answer is D: 3000 mg.

  The mucosa of cheek also has rete pegs, which are not present in the skin.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Thin lamina and non-keratinized mucosa of cheek.

Question: A 9 year old boy presenting with lytic lesion on midshaft tibia. On HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation. Xray is as shown below. What is the likely diagnosis?
Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lytic lesion in the midshaft of the tibia in a 9-year-old boy is suspicious for a benign bone tumor.
  The histopathological features of grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm, and fibroblastic proliferation are suggestive of a giant cell tumor.
  X-ray shows a lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion, which is also consistent with a giant cell tumor.
  Therefore, the likely diagnosis is B: Giant cell tumor.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The X-ray shows a lytic lesion on the midshaft of the tibia.

  Giant cell tumor is a benign tumor that can occur in the bone and is characterized by the presence of giant cells.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare benign bone tumor that usually occurs in the epiphysis of long bones.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that usually occurs in the cortex of long bones and is characterized by the presence of osteoid.
  The age of the patient and the location of the lesion are important clues.
  Based on the age of the patient and the location of the lesion, the most likely diagnosis is osteoid osteoma.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Osteoid osteoma.

Topic: Microbiology
Question: Given below is the diagrammatic representation of a bacterium showing its flagella. Which of the following most closely resembles the organism depicted in the diagram?
Choices:
  A: Leptospria
  B: H. Pylori
  C: Vibrio cholera
  D: Salmonella typhi
Response 0:
Thought:
  The diagram shows a bacterium with peritrichous flagella, which means the flagella are distributed all over the surface of the bacterium.
  Leptospira has axial filaments, which are similar to flagella but are located at the ends of the bacterium.
  H. Pylori has polar flagella, which are located at one end of the bacterium.
  Vibrio cholera has a single polar flagellum.
  Salmonella typhi has peritrichous flagella, similar to the diagram.
  Therefore, the organism depicted in the diagram most closely resembles Salmonella typhi.
Action: Answer("D")

Question: A neonate presents with jaundice and clay coloured stools. Liver biopsy shows giant cells diagnosis is 
Choices:
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia
Response 0:
Thought:
  Jaundice and clay-colored stools are indicative of liver dysfunction.
  Giant cells are indicative of viral hepatitis.
  Neonatal hepatitis is a viral infection that affects the liver of newborns.
  Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a blockage of the bile ducts outside the liver.
  Physiological jaundice is a common condition in newborns.
  Therefore, the neonate most likely has neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Jaundice and clay-colored stools are indicative of liver dysfunction.
  Giant cells are seen in neonatal hepatitis and extrahepatic biliary atresia.
  Physiological jaundice is a normal phenomenon in neonates and does not cause liver dysfunction.
  Therefore, the diagnosis is either neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia or neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice.
  However, since the patient has clay-colored stools, which is a sign of extrahepatic biliary atresia, the diagnosis is neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Pharmacology
Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be cautious while taking drugs as it can be secreted in the milk and can harm the baby.
  Most of the drugs are secreted in the milk, so advice is required.
  Longer half-life drugs will stay in the body for a longer time and can be secreted in the milk.
  Feeding the baby just before the next dose will not prevent the baby from being exposed to the drug.
  It is not advisable to stop feeding the baby as it can lead to malnutrition and other health problems.
  The best advice is to take drugs that are safe for the baby or to avoid drugs if possible.
  Therefore, the answer is A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk.

Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is responsible for the production of heme, which is an important component of hemoglobin.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  The accumulation of what substance in blood reflects this inhibition?
  Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Inhibition of the pathway leads to an accumulation of ALA in the blood.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.

Topic: Pharmacology
Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient is hypertensive and has stage 5 chronic kidney disease.
  The patient has recently been diagnosed with Type 2 diabetes mellitus.
  The patient doesn't want to take injectable insulin.
  The preferred oral hypoglycemic agent should not require any renal dose modification.
  Linagliptin and Vildagliptin are DPP-4 inhibitors and are not renally excreted.
  Repaglinide is metabolized by the liver and does not require renal dose modification.
  Glimepiride is metabolized by the liver but requires renal dose modification.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be either Linagliptin or Vildagliptin.
Action: Answer("A or C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The patient is a 70 years old hypertensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease and Type 2 diabetes mellitus.
  The patient doesn't want to take injectable insulin.
  The patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease, which means the patient's kidneys are functioning at less than 15% of normal capacity.
  In such patients, the use of oral hypoglycemic agents that require renal dose modification is not recommended.
  Linagliptin, Vildagliptin, and Repaglinide are not recommended in patients with renal impairment.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea that is metabolized in the liver and excreted in the urine.
  Glimepiride does not require renal dose modification.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be Glimepiride.

Question: Resolution of IOPA radiograph is?
Choices:
  A: 16 lp
  B: 22 lp
  C: 30 lp
  D: 10 lp
Response 0:
Thought:
  IOPA stands for Intraoral Periapical Radiograph.
  The resolution of an IOPA radiograph is measured in line pairs (lp) per millimeter.
  The higher the number of lp, the better the resolution.
  According to dental literature, the resolution of an IOPA radiograph is between 20-30 lp.
  Therefore, the answer is either C: 30 lp or B: 22 lp.

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is a method where every nth person is selected from a list.
  Simple random sampling is a method where every person has an equal chance of being selected.
  Stratified random sampling is a method where the population is divided into subgroups and a sample is taken from each subgroup.
  Cluster sampling is a method where the population is divided into clusters and a sample is taken from each cluster.
  The question is asking about a method for selecting patients based on potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling is the method that is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a larger population.
  Simple random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a larger population.
  Stratified random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a larger population.
  Cluster sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a larger population.
  The question is asking about a method used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling is a method used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is used to select a sample from a larger population that is arranged in some systematic order.
  Simple random sampling is used to select a sample from a larger population where each individual has an equal chance of being selected.
  Stratified random sampling is used to select a sample from a larger population that can be divided into subgroups or strata.
  Cluster sampling is used to select a sample from a larger population that is divided into clusters or groups.
  The question is asking for a sampling method that is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling is a method that can be used to ensure that the sample includes individuals from each subgroup or stratum, which can help to control for potential factors that may affect the results.
